NPR's Wait Wait... Don't Tell Me!: Show Details and Statistics

« Blog | Mo Rocca, the World's Worst Obstetrician Dot Net? | Individual Show Links No Working? »

Introduction

With a slight obsession over a radio program called, "Wait Wait... Don't Tell Me!" (also known as: WWDTM), I have started collecting various information regarding the radio program and storing the information in a database. The inspiration for creating my own statistics and page came from another avid Wait Wait fan, which I also used as a basis to help collect information for the initial shows hosted by Dan Coffey.

Please note that I am not affiliated or associated, nor do I receive any direct or indirect support from NPR, Chicago Public Radio, or Urgent Haircut Productions. If you really like this site and find it useful, you can help support the ongoing maintenance, hosting and maintenance by purchasing anything from Amazon.com using my referral link or from my Amazon.com Wish Lists.

If you have any comments, corrections or questions, please feel free to post them under the Plans for Wait Wait Statistics Site blog post on my website.

Content

This page is broken into four sections, one that details each of the program's show statistics and one that details the statistics for each panelist.

Show Statistics

The following tables contain various details for each of the shows entered into the database. Instead of collecting every minute detail of each show, show descriptions only contain high-level details and do not include information about the panelist rounds or the Lightning Fill-in-the-Blank round. The "Are You an NPR Geek?" is also known as the NPR Geek Game.

The panelist names are color coded based on how each one finished the "Lightning Fill-in-the-Blank" round. The color scheme used is:

  • Dark Red: First place
  • Red: Tied for first place
  • Dark Green: Second place
  • Green: Tied for second place
  • Default: Third place or Not Applicable (for "Best of" shows)

Number of shows in database: 881

2014-01-25  The edited version of the show only had 7 of 8 questions for Hannibal Buress, with five being answered correctly. Carl stated that Hannibal answered 6 correctly, meaning that the question cut was answered correctly or there was a mis-count. If Hannibal had answered only 5 questions correct, he would have had a total of 11 points.

When Peter asked Carl how many questions Jessi had to answer to win, Carl stated that she would need "4 to tie, 5 to win outright". That would only be true if Brian Babylon was in the lead with 12 points against Hannibal's 11 points, not 13 as Carl tallied. There would be no way for Jessi to tie with Hannibal due to Jessi starting the round with an even number of points while Hannibal started and ended with an odd number.

In the end, it didn't matter for Jessi had more than enough correct answers to surpass either Hannibal or Brian. But, it does affect placement for Hannibal and Brian as their placement would actually get swapped.

2014-02-08  During the discussion about the conditions that journalists saw in Sochi prior to the opening ceremony at the Sochi Olympics and comparing them in the US, Tom started to describe Motel 6 without using their name; Tom Bodett is famous for being Motel 6's spokesperson.

Right after Peter explained the premise of the Bluff the Listener round to the listener, the listener asked if Roxanne was on the panel. When it was confirmed, the listener stated that he didn't have to go through the "charade" and picked Roxanne. This is in reference the number of times where Roxanne's bluff is chosen due to the believability of her stories, even if those stories are not correct ones. Peter Guralnick made a reference to this right before his first Not My Job question.

Peter Sagal accidentally said Ginger Roberts instead of Ginger Rogers. Both Peters had fun with this throughout the third Not My Job question.

2014-03-08  While the panelists were discussing the recent changes to the SAT exam, Faith Salie decided to use some elaborate words that one might find the SAT exams, stating that everyone uses such words.

During the first panelist round, Peter was about to give Faith a hint and he said "here's your excuse" instead of "here's your hint". Hilarity ensued.

When Peter was reading the first Not My Job question, he said "In 2011, an undercover sting, ha, run by...". The "ha" was in reference to The Police's front man Sting. After answering the last Not My Job question, Steward sung a dramatic tune as Peter was about to say that the answer was correct. While Peter rejected Steward's answer and started to explain the correct answer, Steward sung a "fail" tune in response.

Not too much laughter (or groaning) happened when Peter Sagal used "rhymean" as the Listener Limerick Challenge pun prior to the second panelist round. Peter then stated, "that one was good".

The panelist placement methodology used is the Standard competition ranking; in which, for a given show, if two panelists are tied for first then the other panelist is designated as being third.
